Al-Ghazali's Fourfold Classification: The Perished and the Saved
Al-Ghazali's fourfold classification with definitions of the perished and saved.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's fourfold classification of people and the definitions of the perished (halik) and the saved (naji).

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali divides all people into four fate-based categories: perished, saved, happy, perfectly happy.

In this opening passage, the author sets the stage for discussing theological factions by presenting al-Ghazali's classification of humanity. According to this classification, after Allah's eternal decree, people fall into four categories, each with a distinct state in the Hereafter. The passage defines the first two: those who perish due to rejecting Islam, and those who are saved despite holding misguidance that does not remove them from the faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic text from 'وقد قضى المولى' to the end, focusing on the four categories mentioned and the definitions of the first two.
Notice that the author does not define the happy and perfectly happy here.
2
Identify the two defined categories
Find the definitions of 'al-halik' and 'al-naji'. Compare their conditions: one rejects Islam entirely, the other professes faith but holds some misguidance.
3
Reflect on the classification's purpose
Consider why al-Ghazali includes a middle category (the saved) between the perished and the happy. How does this relate to the sectarian context?
The author mentions 'factions of desires' (ahl al-ahwa') as examples of the saved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
جلَّ الحي القيوم، جبَّار السماوات والأرض، سبوح قدوس رب الملائكة والروح، له الحمد على ما منَّ من نعيمِ معرفته وأجزل العطاء بروح وريحان قربه، والصلاة والسلام على أمينه على وحيه من ابتعثه للخلق رحمة، سيدنا ومولانا محمد بن عبد الله، وآله وصحبه ومن والاه إلى يوم الدين.
وبعد:
فيقول الحقُّ سبحانه: ﴿أَفَمَنْ أَسَّسَ بُنْيَانَهُ عَلَى تَقْوَى مِنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانٍ خَيْرٌ أَم مَنْ أَسَّسَ بُنْيَانَهُ عَلَى شَفَا جُرُفٍ هَارٍ﴾ [التوبة: ١٠٩].
وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «عَلَيْكُمْ بِالْجَمَاعَةِ، وَإِيَّاكُمْ وَالْفُرْقَةَ» (١).
وعقد إمام المحدثين أبو عبد الله البخاري في صحيحه باباً فقال: (بابُ قولِ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا تزال طائفة من أمتي ظاهرين على الحق يقاتلون»)، ثم فسر هذه الطائفة فقال: (وهم أهل العلم)، فللعلماء أعظم الجهاد.
وقد قضى المولى جل جلاله باختلاف الأمة مختارين، حتى صارت نحلاً وفرقاً ومذاهب، والناس بعد هذه القسمة الأزلية التي لله فيها الحجة البالغة على عباده أقسام أربعة كما يرى حجة الإسلام الغزالي في عموم كتبه: هالك في الآخرة، وناج، وسعيد، وكامل السعادة.
فالهالك: من أعرض ونأى بجانبه واختار غير سبيل الهدى، ولم يرتض الإسلام ديناً.
والناجي: كل من قال: لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله، وأقر بكل معلوم من دين الإسلام بالضرورة، غير أنه جمع إلى هذا ضلالاً في العلميات والعمليات اعتقاداً وفقهاً مما لا يبلغ به حد الخروج عن الدين؛ كفرق الأهواء المشهورة.
(١) رواه الترمذي (٢١٦٥) من حديث سيدنا عمر رضي الله عنه.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Majestic is the Living, the Self-Subsisting, the Compeller of the heavens and the earth, the All-Holy, the All-Pure, Lord of the angels and the Spirit. To Him belongs praise for what He has bestowed of the bliss of knowing Him and has given abundantly with the spirit and fragrance of His nearness. And blessings and peace be upon His trustworthy one over His revelation, whom He sent as a mercy to creation, our master and patron Muhammad ibn Abdullah, and his family, companions, and those who follow him until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: Allah, the Exalted, says: 'Is he who founds his building upon fear of Allah and [seeking] His pleasure better, or he who founds his building upon the brink of a crumbling precipice?' [At-Tawbah 109]. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Hold fast to the community, and beware of division' (1). The imam of the hadith scholars, Abu Abdullah al-Bukhari, in his Sahih, titled a chapter and said: 'Chapter: The Prophet's saying: "A faction of my community will continue to prevail upon the truth, fighting..."' Then he interpreted this faction and said: 'They are the people of knowledge.' So for the scholars is the greatest jihad. Allah, exalted is His majesty, decreed the differences of the community by choice, so that it became sects, factions, and schools. And people after this eternal division, in which Allah has the conclusive argument against His servants, are four categories, as the Proof of Islam al-Ghazali sees in most of his books: the perished in the Hereafter, the saved, the happy, and the perfectly happy. The perished: the one who turned away and withdrew to his side, and chose other than the path of guidance, and did not accept Islam as a religion. The saved: everyone who said 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' and affirmed every necessarily known matter of the religion of Islam, but he combined with this misguidance in theoretical and practical matters, in belief and jurisprudence, which does not reach the level of exiting the religion; like the well-known factions of desires. (1) Narrated by at-Tirmidhi (2165) from the hadith of our master Umar, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the author's introduction. It begins with the basmalah and praise of Allah, acknowledging Him as the Living, Self-Subsisting, Compeller, Holy, and Lord of angels and the Spirit. The author thanks Allah for the blessing of knowing Him and for spiritual gifts. Then he sends blessings on the Prophet Muhammad, his family, and companions. After the 'amma ba'd (to proceed), he quotes a Quranic verse (At-Tawbah 9:109) contrasting those who build on piety versus those who build on a crumbling edge. He then cites a hadith commanding adherence to the community (jama'ah) and warning against division. He mentions al-Bukhari's chapter on the enduring faction of the ummah that fights upon the truth, which al-Bukhari interpreted as the people of knowledge, indicating the high status of scholars. The author then states that Allah decreed differences among the ummah, resulting in various sects and schools. He introduces al-Ghazali's classification of people into four categories: perished (halik) in the Hereafter, saved (naji), happy (sa'id), and perfectly happy (kamil al-sa'adah). He elaborates only the first two: the perished are those who reject and turn away from Islam; the saved are those who profess faith and affirm necessary matters but have misguidance in theoretical and practical aspects that does not amount to apostasy, exemplified by factions of desires (ahl al-ahwa'). The footnote cites at-Tirmidhi for the hadith. This passage sets the stage: the author will later focus on the saved and the happy, perhaps in the context of theological sects.

Key Terms
هالك
ناجي
سعيد
كامل السعادة
الغزالي
أهل الأهواء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The saved are those who are free from all error in belief and practice.
Correction: Al-Ghazali defines the saved as those who have misguidance in some theoretical or practical matters, as long as it does not reach apostasy. They are not perfectly correct.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ghazali as quoted, what defines the 'saved' (الناجي)?
A) One who professes Islam but deviates in some beliefs without leaving the religion.
B) One who completely abandons Islam.
C) One who is perfectly happy in the Hereafter.
D) One who is among the scholars fighting for the truth.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali teaches that salvation begins with the shahada and affirmation of necessary religious knowledge, but misguidance that falls short of apostasy still places one among the saved rather than the perished.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You recite the shahada and claim to affirm all necessary religious matters—but where in your life do you knowingly cling to a mistaken belief or practice that falls short of apostasy? Are you content to remain among the 'saved' with that error, or will you uproot it to seek perfect happiness?
?
Al-Ghazali says the perished are those who actively turned away and did not accept Islam. But you were born into it—have you ever truly chosen the path of guidance, or do you follow it passively? What would it mean for you to willfully ‘turn away’ even slightly in your heart?
?
You are either among the perished, saved, happy, or perfectly happy. Which do you expect to be if you died tonight? If you are not sure, what specific step will you take today to move closer to perfect happiness, based on what this lesson teaches?

The Foundation of Knowledge and Unity
Author cites Quran and hadith to establish the significance of knowledge and unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses Quranic and prophetic citations to establish the importance of knowledge and communal unity as the foundation for correct belief.

Core Idea
Unity and knowledge are intertwined; the saved group is the people of knowledge.

The author opens his work by grounding it in the Quran and Sunnah. He quotes a verse contrasting a sound foundation with a crumbling one, and a hadith urging adherence to the community. Then he cites al-Bukhari's identification of the victorious group as the scholars. This lesson examines how these texts frame the entire discussion of correct belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice the flow from praise to citation of Quran and hadith.
The basmala and praise set a reverent tone.
2
Analyze the Quranic verse
Examine verse 9:109 about building on taqwa vs. a crumbling precipice. Understand how it implies the author's work is built on a sound foundation.
This verse is a metaphor for the importance of correct belief.
3
Examine the hadith and Bukhari's interpretation
Read the hadith urging unity and warning against division. Note al-Bukhari's interpretation that the victorious group is the scholars.
This directly ties knowledge to the saved group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسۡمِ ٱللَّهِ ٱلرَّحۡمَٰنِ ٱلرَّحِيمِ. جلَّ الحي القيوم، جَبَّار السماوات والأرض، سبوح قدوس رب الملائكة والروح، له الحمد على ما مَنَّ مِن نعيمِ معرفته وأجزل العطاء بروح وريحان قربه، والصلاة والسلام على أمينه على وحيه الذي ابتعثه للخلق رحمة، سيدنا ومولانا محمد بن عبد الله، وآله وصحبه ومن والاه إلى يوم الدين. وبعد: فيقول الحق سبحانه: (أَفَمَنْ أَسَّسَ بُنْيَانَهُ عَلَى تَقْوَى مِنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانٍ خَيْرٌ أَم مَنْ أَسَّسَ بُنْيَانَهُ عَلَى شَفَا جُرُفٍ هَارٍ) [التوبة: ١٠٩]. وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «عَلَيْكُمْ بِالجَمَاعَةِ، وَإِيَّاكُمْ وَالفُرْقَةِ» (1). وعقد إمام المحدثين أبو عبد الله البخاري في صحيحه باباً فقال: (بَابُ قَوْلِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: لاَ تَزَالُ طَائِفَةٌ مِنْ أُمَّتِي ظَاهِرِينَ عَلَى الحَقِّ يُقَاتِلُونَ)، ثم فسَّر هذه الطائفة فقال: (وَهُمْ أَهْلُ العِلْمِ)، فللعلماء أعظم الجهاد.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Mighty, the Self-Subsisting, the Compeller of the heavens and the earth, the Exalted, the Holy, Lord of the angels and the spirit. To Him be praise for what He has granted of the bliss of knowledge of Him and He has given abundantly with the spirit and basil of His nearness. And blessings and peace be upon the trustee of His revelation, whom He sent as a mercy to creation, our master and lord Muhammad ibn Abdullah, and upon his family, his companions, and those who follow him until the Day of Judgment. To proceed: Allah the Exalted says: 'Is he who founded his building upon taqwa of Allah and [His] pleasure better, or he who founded his building upon the brink of a crumbling precipice?' [At-Tawba 109]. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Cling to the community, and beware of division.' (1). And the imam of hadith scholars, Abu Abdullah al-Bukhari, in his Sahih, made a chapter and said: 'The statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): "A group from my ummah will not cease to be manifest upon the truth, fighting." Then he interpreted this group and said: 'They are the people of knowledge.' So the scholars have the greatest jihad.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the book. It begins with the basmala and praise of Allah, then quotes a Quranic verse about building on taqwa vs. on a precipice, implying that the work's foundation is sound. Then the hadith urging adherence to the community (jama'ah) and warning against division. Then al-Bukhari's chapter heading and his interpretation that the victorious group is the people of knowledge. The author uses these to establish the importance of knowledge and unity, setting the stage for the discussion of correct belief and the saved group.

Key Terms
طائفة
الجماعة
أهل العلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The passage includes the hadith about the 73 sects.
Correction: The hadith here is about clinging to the community, not about the 73 sects. The victorious group is identified as the people of knowledge.

Checkpoint
What did al-Bukhari interpret the victorious group to be?
A) The scholars
B) The martyrs
C) The rulers
D) The wealthy

Key Takeaway
The author establishes that the foundation of correct belief is knowledge and unity, as evidenced by the Quran and prophetic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Prophet commanded clinging to the community and warned against division. Where in your life have you contributed to division—whether in your family, mosque, or online? Will you sincerely repent and actively seek unity, even with those you disagree with?
?
Al-Bukhari identified the victorious group as the people of knowledge. Is your pursuit of knowledge about Allah and His religion consistent with being among that group? What specific, concrete step can you take this week to increase your share of beneficial knowledge?
?
The Quran contrasts building on taqwa and divine pleasure with building on a crumbling precipice. Honestly examine the foundation of your faith: is it built on genuine taqwa and seeking Allah's pleasure, or have you been careless, relying on shaky foundations? What must change starting today?

The Harmony of Reason and Revelation
Sanusi explains the unifying methodology of Ahl al-Sunna in balancing reason and revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Sunna unify reason and transmitted revelation, avoiding the extremes of literalism and esotericism.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna build on both reason and revelation, removing any conflict between them.

In this passage, Imam al-Sanusi describes the distinctive method of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. He explains that their foundations are firm and combine both rational and transmitted evidence, thus avoiding the pitfalls of those who reject reason or demean revelation. This lesson explores this balanced approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the key phrases about reason and transmission.
Pay attention to the phrase 'جامعة بين طريقي العقل والنقل'.
2
Identify the two extremes
The author mentions ẓāhiriyya (literalism) and bāṭiniyya (esotericism). Understand what each means and why they are problematic.
Ẓāhiriyya rejects rational interpretation; bāṭiniyya demeans the apparent meaning.
3
Reflect on the harmony
Consider why combining both paths is considered a great characteristic of Ahl al-Sunna.
4
Connect to later branches
Notice that this harmony forms the basis for the soundness of their branches, which will be discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المتأمِّلُ فيما عليه أهل السنة والجماعة يرى أنهم قد شيَّدوا فروعهم على أصول راسخة ثابتة، جامعة بين طريقي العقل والنقل؛ فلا يرى خلافاً بينهما، وهذه خصيصة عظيمة، فلا يتشكّى مستبصر من حيف أحدهما على الآخر، فانتفتْ بذلك ظاهريَّةٌ يأنفُها العقل، وباطنية تزري بحق النقل. ولمَّا كان للفروع حكمُ الأصول، وكانت أصول أهل السنة العقديَّة (أصول الدين وعلم الكلام) والفقهيَّة (أصول الفقه وأصول مصطلح الحديث)، والتربوية (أصول التصوف) أصولاً صحيحةً جليَّة الدليل، كانت الفروعُ المستنبطة عنها صحيحة بالحجة والبرهان على تفاوت بينها؛ إذ نرى عامة المسائل العلمية الاعتقادية برهانية الدليل والمسائل العمليَّة الفقهية دائرةً بين البرهاني وما يغلب فيه الظن غلبة تقترب من اليقين، إلا في فروع ليست بالكثيرة أمام حجم المستنبطات قد كانت في محل الاجتهاد، غير أن الأيام أظهرت أنها محصورة ضمن مذاهب أربعة قد تلقتها الأمة بالقبول، حتى كادت تحكم بخطأ ما سواها، ولا سيما بعد استقرار الفقه وأصوله، وغياب أهلية الاجتهاد (١).
Then the contemplator of what Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are upon sees that they have built their branches upon firm, established foundations, combining the two paths of reason and transmission; so he sees no conflict between them. This is a great characteristic. So a discerning person does not complain of oppression from one upon the other. Thus, both literalism (ẓāhiriyya) which reason abhors, and esotericism (bāṭiniyya) which demeans the right of transmission, are eliminated. And since branches have the same rule as foundations, and the foundations of Ahl al-Sunna – creedal (principles of religion and ilm al-kalam), legal (principles of fiqh and principles of hadith terminology), and educational (principles of tasawwuf) – are authentic foundations with clear evidence, the branches derived from them are correct by proof and demonstration, though varying among themselves. For we see that most theoretical creedal issues are demonstrative (burhānī) in evidence, while practical legal issues vary between the demonstrative and what is predominantly probable to a degree close to certainty, except in some branches which are not many compared to the volume of derived rulings, which were subject to ijtihad. However, time has shown that they are confined within four schools which the ummah has accepted, to the point that they almost judge as erroneous anything outside them, especially after the stabilization of fiqh and its principles, and the disappearance of the qualification for ijtihad.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage explains the methodology of Ahl al-Sunna. First, they combine reason and revealed texts, avoiding both extremes of literalism (that rejects reason) and esotericism (that demeans revelation). Then it discusses that the foundations (usul) are sound, and thus the branches (furu') derived are sound. It distinguishes between creedal issues, which are demonstratively proven, and juristic issues, which range from demonstrative to probabilistic. The author notes that the four madhhabs have been accepted by the ummah and ijtihad has effectively closed. This passage affirms the authority of the four schools and the rational basis of creed.

Key Terms
أصول راسخة
العقل والنقل
ظاهريَّة
باطنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-Sunna are purely traditionalists who reject reason.
Correction: This passage shows they combine reason and transmission, and consider literalism as something reason abhors. So they are not purely traditionalist.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is eliminated by combining reason and transmission?
A) Conflict between scholars
B) Literalism and esotericism
C) All differences of opinion
D) Need for ijtihad

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna's methodology harmonizes reason and revelation, avoiding extremes of literalism and esotericism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, are there areas where you feel a tension between what reason suggests and what revelation teaches? How does this passage challenge you to seek harmony rather than pick a side? What concrete step will you take this week to build on both foundations?
?
Have you ever dismissed a religious ruling as 'unreasonable' without trying to understand its wisdom? Or have you ever clung to a literal interpretation that actually contradicts sound reason? Which extreme are you more prone to, and how can this lesson's balance reshape your approach?
?
Think of a difficult issue you've faced where scripture seemed to conflict with logic. Instead of forcing a resolution, did you surrender your intellect or your trust in revelation? This passage calls for a third way: holding both without oppression. Are you willing to sit in that tension until understanding comes? What is one practical situation where you will apply this harmony today?

Sound Foundations and the Four Madhhabs
Sanusi discusses the relationship between foundations and branches, and the acceptance of four legal schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sound foundations of Ahl al-Sunna lead to sound branches, and why the four madhhabs have achieved near-consensus.

Core Idea
Sound foundations yield sound branches, with creedal issues being demonstrative and juristic issues probable, leading to acceptance of four schools.

Having established the methodology, Sanusi now explains that because the foundations (uṣūl) of Ahl al-Sunna are sound, their derived branches are also sound. He distinguishes between creedal and juristic issues in terms of certainty, and concludes that the four madhhabs have been accepted by the ummah, effectively closing the door of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation from 'ولمَّا كان للفروع' to the end.
Focus on the logical flow from foundations to branches.
2
Understand the principle
Branches have the same rule as foundations – if foundations are sound, branches are sound. Identify the three categories of foundations mentioned.
The categories are creedal, legal, and educational.
3
Distinguish certainty levels
Notice that creedal issues are demonstrative (burhānī), while juristic issues vary from demonstrative to probable (close to certainty). This explains why some rulings are open to ijtihad.
4
The role of the four schools
The passage explains that despite some ijtihad, the four schools have become the accepted frameworks, and the qualification for independent ijtihad has effectively disappeared.
Think about why acceptance by the ummah is significant.
5
Reflect on closure of ijtihad
Consider why the author states that the four schools are so accepted that they almost judge anything outside as erroneous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المتأمِّلُ فيما عليه أهل السنة والجماعة يرى أنهم قد شيَّدوا فروعهم على أصول راسخة ثابتة، جامعة بين طريقي العقل والنقل؛ فلا يرى خلافاً بينهما، وهذه خصيصة عظيمة، فلا يتشكّى مستبصر من حيف أحدهما على الآخر، فانتفتْ بذلك ظاهريَّةٌ يأنفُها العقل، وباطنية تزري بحق النقل. ولمَّا كان للفروع حكمُ الأصول، وكانت أصول أهل السنة العقديَّة (أصول الدين وعلم الكلام) والفقهيَّة (أصول الفقه وأصول مصطلح الحديث)، والتربوية (أصول التصوف) أصولاً صحيحةً جليَّة الدليل، كانت الفروعُ المستنبطة عنها صحيحة بالحجة والبرهان على تفاوت بينها؛ إذ نرى عامة المسائل العلمية الاعتقادية برهانية الدليل والمسائل العمليَّة الفقهية دائرةً بين البرهاني وما يغلب فيه الظن غلبة تقترب من اليقين، إلا في فروع ليست بالكثيرة أمام حجم المستنبطات قد كانت في محل الاجتهاد، غير أن الأيام أظهرت أنها محصورة ضمن مذاهب أربعة قد تلقتها الأمة بالقبول، حتى كادت تحكم بخطأ ما سواها، ولا سيما بعد استقرار الفقه وأصوله، وغياب أهلية الاجتهاد (١).
Then the contemplator of what Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are upon sees that they have built their branches upon firm, established foundations, combining the two paths of reason and transmission; so he sees no conflict between them. This is a great characteristic. So a discerning person does not complain of oppression from one upon the other. Thus, both literalism (ẓāhiriyya) which reason abhors, and esotericism (bāṭiniyya) which demeans the right of transmission, are eliminated. And since branches have the same rule as foundations, and the foundations of Ahl al-Sunna – creedal (principles of religion and ilm al-kalam), legal (principles of fiqh and principles of hadith terminology), and educational (principles of tasawwuf) – are authentic foundations with clear evidence, the branches derived from them are correct by proof and demonstration, though varying among themselves. For we see that most theoretical creedal issues are demonstrative (burhānī) in evidence, while practical legal issues vary between the demonstrative and what is predominantly probable to a degree close to certainty, except in some branches which are not many compared to the volume of derived rulings, which were subject to ijtihad. However, time has shown that they are confined within four schools which the ummah has accepted, to the point that they almost judge as erroneous anything outside them, especially after the stabilization of fiqh and its principles, and the disappearance of the qualification for ijtihad.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage explains the methodology of Ahl al-Sunna. First, they combine reason and revealed texts, avoiding both extremes of literalism (that rejects reason) and esotericism (that demeans revelation). Then it discusses that the foundations (usul) are sound, and thus the branches (furu') derived are sound. It distinguishes between creedal issues, which are demonstratively proven, and juristic issues, which range from demonstrative to probabilistic. The author notes that the four madhhabs have been accepted by the ummah and ijtihad has effectively closed. This passage affirms the authority of the four schools and the rational basis of creed.

Key Terms
أصول الدين
علم الكلام
أصول الفقه
مصطلح الحديث
أصول التصوف
برهان
اجتهاد
مذاهب أربعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Islamic rulings are equally certain and not open to ijtihad.
Correction: The passage clarifies that juristic issues vary in certainty, with many being probable, and a few were subject to ijtihad.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of most theoretical creedal issues (المسائل العلمية الاعتقادية)?
A) They are probabilistic
B) They are demonstrative (burhānī)
C) They are based on ijtihad
D) They are not important

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna's sound foundations ensure derived branches are correct, with creedal issues proven demonstratively and juristic issues accepted within four orthodox schools.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow ahl al-sunna—are your foundations sound? How do you know? This lesson says that only sound foundations produce correct branches. What foundation—whether in belief, practice, or spirituality—do you lack clear evidence for, and what will you do to strengthen it today?
?
The ummah has confined ijtihad to four schools. Do you ever feel tempted to follow a view outside these schools because it is easier? How does the lesson's emphasis on the acceptance of the schools challenge you to submit to scholarly authority rather than personal desire?
?
This lesson distinguishes demonstrative creedal issues from probable juristic ones. In your daily practice, do you treat matters of fiqh with the same certainty as matters of aqeedah? Reflect on a specific instance where you held a juristic opinion dogmatically—how can you align with the proper level of certainty taught here?

Majority vs. Truth in Creed
Clarifies that the 'sawad al-a'zam' in hadith does not apply to usul al-din; creed requires independent proofs, citing al-Juwayni.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why creedal matters cannot be determined by majority opinion and why rational proofs are necessary.

Core Idea
Truth in creed is not decided by numbers; evidence is the only foundation.

A common hadith urges adherence to the 'great majority,' but does that mean we should follow the crowd in everything? The scholar al-Juwayni clarifies that this hadith does not apply to the core beliefs of Islam. Instead, creed requires independent proofs, not popularity. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the direct quote from Imam al-Juwayni.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that the 'great multitude' in the hadith is not about usul al-din. Underline this in the translation.
3
Understand al-Juwayni's argument
Al-Juwayni gives two reasons: the majority of disbelievers is larger, and the early Muslims were few. Find these in the text.
This shows that numerical majority does not indicate truth.
4
Recognize the implication
The conclusion is that belief must be purified by proofs and demonstrations. Ask yourself why this is necessary for creed.
This connects to the learning objective.
5
Reflect on the methodology
Consider how this principle supports the use of kalam (rational theology) in defending and understanding core beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس المقصود من السواد الأعظم في الحديث الشريف ما كان في أصول الدين؛ ولذلك قال الإمام الجويني: (لا) معوّل على السواد الأعظم في أصل الدين؛ فإن سواد الكفرة أعظم من سوادنا، ولقد كان الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم في صدر الإسلام في شرذمة قليلة العدد، وليس المعنى باتباع السواد الأعظم الاتباع في أصول الدين)(٢)، ومن هنا وجب تحريرُ الاعتقاد بالحجج والبراهين فلا يُرتضى إلا الاعتقاد الراسخ الذي
And the intended meaning of the 'great multitude' (sawād al-aʻẓam) in the noble hadith is not [about] what is in the principles of religion. Therefore, Imam al-Juwayni said: 'No reliance is placed on the great multitude in the foundation of religion, for the multitude of disbelievers is greater than our multitude, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in the early days of Islam was in a small band.' And the meaning is not that following the great multitude is [the way] in the principles of religion. From here, it is necessary to purify belief with proofs and demonstrations, and nothing is accepted except firm belief which...
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage addresses a common misunderstanding about the hadith that says 'adhere to the great majority.' The author clarifies that this does not apply to foundational creedal matters (usul al-din), because truth is not determined by numbers. He cites al-Juwayni, who argues that the majority of people at many times have been upon falsehood, and the early Muslims were few. Therefore, in matters of creed, one must rely on evidence and proof, not on popularity. This reinforces the importance of ilm al-kalam and rational demonstration in theology.

أصول الدين
الإمام الجويني
تحرير الاعتقاد
حجج وبراهين

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about adhering to the great majority applies to all matters including creed.
Correction: The hadith does not apply to foundational creedal matters; truth in creed is determined by evidence, not majority.

Checkpoint

A) The majority is always wrong
B) The majority of early Muslims were disbelievers
C) The multitude of disbelievers is greater than believers
D) The hadith is weak

Key Takeaway
In matters of creed, truth is not determined by majority but by sound proofs and arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever hold a belief simply because it is popular among Muslims around you, without having examined the evidence for it? What is one belief you are afraid to question because it might make you stand alone?

?
If everyone around you held a certain creed, but you knew the evidence pointed elsewhere, would you have the courage to choose truth over numbers? What is stopping you from seeking proof for your own convictions right now?

The Fortunate Believer and Perfect Felicity
The author defines al-sa'id and kamil al-sa'ada, identifying Ahl al-Sunna as the people of perfect felicity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the fortunate believer (al-sa'id) and the concept of perfect felicity (kamil al-sa'ada) as belonging to Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.

Core Idea
Perfect felicity is for those who follow the truth with proof and adhere to the Prophet's way.

In this passage, the author defines two key terms: the fortunate believer and perfect felicity. He explains that the fortunate one is not just any Muslim but one who attaches himself to truth through proof and follows the way of the Prophet and Companions without innovation. Perfect felicity is a higher rank attained by the saints (awliya) of Allah, specifically identified as Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. This lesson establishes the foundation for understanding the Sunni vision of salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the first part of the source text (up to 'wa hum ahl al-sunna wa al-jama'a') and its translation. Notice how the author defines al-sa'id and then kamil al-sa'ada.
2
Understand the definition of al-sa'id
Identify the three conditions: (1) a Muslim who attaches to truth by proof, (2) follows the Prophet and Companions, (3) does not change or alter, though he may not excel in supererogatory acts.
The phrase 'ghayr annahu la yusabiq bi al-khayrat' means he is not necessarily the foremost in good deeds.
3
Understand perfect felicity
Notice that perfect felicity is reserved for the awliya who have reached ihsan, and they are explicitly identified as Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
4
Ask: Why is this identification important?
Reflect on the significance of defining orthodoxy by this standard. The commentary explains that this sets apart Sunni Muslims from others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسعيدُ : المسلم الذي أضاف نفسه للحقِّ بالحجّة والبرهان، وكان على ما عليه النبي الله وأصحابه الكرام، ولم يُغيّر ولم يبدّل، غير أنه لا يُسابق بالخيرات. و كامل السعادة هو من أولياء الله تعالى الذين بلغوا رتبة الإحسان وهم أهل السنة والجماعة. ثم المتأمِّلُ فيما عليه أهل السنة والجماعة يرى أنهم قد شيَّدوا فروعهم على أصول راسخة ثابتة، جامعة بين طريقي العقل والنقل ؛ فلا يرى خلافاً بينهما، وهذه خصيصة عظيمة، فلا يتشكّى مستبصر من حيف أحدهما على الآخر، فانتفتْ بذلك ظاهريَّةٌ يأنفُها العقل، وباطنية تزري بحق النقل.
The fortunate one is the Muslim who attaches himself to the truth by proof and demonstration, and who follows what the Prophet of Allah and his noble Companions were upon, and does not change or alter, except that he does not hasten to do good deeds. And the perfect felicity is from the friends of Allah, exalted is He, who have attained the station of excellence (ihsan), and they are the people of the Sunna and the community (Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a). Then the one who contemplates what Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are upon sees that they have built their branches upon firm, established foundations, combining the two paths of reason and transmission; he sees no contradiction between them, and this is a great characteristic. So a clear-sighted person does not complain of injustice of one over the other. Thus, by that, there is eliminated a literalism (zahiriyya) that reason abhors, and an esotericism (batiniyya) that degrades the right of transmission.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms and highlights the distinctive methodology of Ahl al-Sunna. The author first defines 'al-sa'id' (the fortunate one) as a Muslim who attains truth through proof and demonstration, adheres to the way of the Prophet and the Companions without innovation, although he may not excel in supererogatory acts. Then he defines 'kamil al-sa'ada' (perfect felicity) as the status of the awliya (saints) who have reached the rank of ihsan, identifying them specifically as Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. Next, the author points out a key feature of Ahl al-Sunna: when one examines their doctrines, one sees that they have built their subsidiary branches on firm principles that harmonize reason and revelation. This is a great virtue because a fair-minded observer finds no conflict between the two sources; thus, two extreme positions are avoided: a literalist approach (zahiriyya) that reason rejects, and an esoteric approach (batiniyya) that undermines the authority of revealed texts. The passage establishes the balanced, rational-textual methodology that characterizes orthodox Sunni Islam.

Key Terms
سعيد (sa'id)
كامل السعادة (kamil al-sa'ada)
أولياء (awliya)
أهل السنة والجماعة (Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any Muslim who believes is automatically a fortunate believer with perfect felicity.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between a fortunate believer (who may not excel in good deeds) and the perfect felicity of the awliya (saints), who are specifically Ahl al-Sunna.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the term 'kamil al-sa'ada' (perfect felicity) specifically refer to?
A) Any Muslim who performs many good deeds
B) The friends of Allah who have attained the station of ihsan, i.e., Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a
C) The early generations of Muslims regardless of their sect
D) Those who follow only reason and reject tradition

Key Takeaway
Perfect felicity is the special rank of Ahl al-Sunna saints who combine faith with excellence in worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you attach yourself to the truth with proof and demonstration, or do you follow your desires? Examine your heart: have you truly submitted to the evidence, or do you only accept what suits you?
?
The fortunate believer does not hasten to good deeds—but have you used this as an excuse for laziness? Where do you stand between the two categories: are you striving for perfect felicity or content with mere fortune?
?
Ahl al-Sunna are described as the friends of Allah who have attained ihsan. Are you content to be merely a Muslim in name, or do you yearn to be among those who worship as if seeing Allah? What is one habit you must change to move from sa'id to kamil al-sa'ada?

The Methodology of Ahl al-Sunna: Balancing Reason and Revelation
The author describes the balanced methodology of Ahl al-Sunna combining reason and revelation, avoiding literalism and esotericism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinctive methodology of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in harmonizing reason and revelation, avoiding the extremes of literalism and esotericism.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna combine reason and revelation, rejecting both blind literalism and esoteric allegorism.

This passage highlights a key characteristic of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a: their approach builds subsidiary doctrines on firm foundational principles that integrate both rational and transmitted evidence. This balanced methodology ensures that neither reason nor revelation is compromised. The author contrasts this with two extremes: zahiriyya (crude literalism) and batiniyya (esoteric interpretation that undermines textual authority). This lesson unpacks this unique synthesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the second part of the source text starting from 'thumma al-muta'ammin' and its translation. Notice the claim about Ahl al-Sunna's methodology.
2
Identify the two foundations
The passage says they built their branches on firm foundations combining reason ('aql) and transmission (naql). Understand that both are essential.
3
Understand the two extremes avoided
The author mentions zahiriyya (literalism) that reason abhors, and batiniyya (esotericism) that degrades revelation. Ahl al-Sunna avoid both.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this balance is important. It shows that Sunni theology respects both intellect and scripture, appealing to rational minds while preserving revelation.

Source Text

Branches Depend on Roots
The author establishes that branches follow foundations and discusses the soundness of Ahl al-Sunna's foundations and derived branches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the branches of knowledge derive their authority from their foundations and how this applies to the various disciplines of Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
Branches follow the ruling of their roots.

Before we can discuss specific theological issues, we must establish the relationship between foundational principles and the branches derived from them. This passage explains that because the foundations of Ahl al-Sunna are sound, the derived rulings are also sound, though they vary in certainty. The author also notes how time has confined the branches of fiqh to four accepted schools.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author asserts a general principle about branches and foundations.
Pay attention to the list of different types of foundations mentioned.
2
Identify the types of foundations
The passage mentions three categories of foundations: creedal (usul al-din and kalam), jurisprudential (usul al-fiqh and hadith methodology), and spiritual (usul al-tasawwuf). Note that all are said to be sound.
3
Reflect on the variation of branches
The author says derived branches vary in certainty: doctrinal issues are demonstrative, while practical fiqh issues range from demonstrative to probable. Think about why this variation exists.
Consider that ijtihad was allowed in a few branches, but now confined to four schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمَّا كان للفروع حكمُ الأصول، وكانت أصول أهل السنة العقديَّة (أصول الدين وعلم الكلام والفقهيَّةُ (أصول الفقه وأصول مصطلح الحديث)، والتربوية (أصول التصوف) أصولاً صحيحةً جليَّة الدليل، كانت الفروعُ المستنبطة عنها صحيحة بالحجة والبرهان على تفاوت بينها ؛ إذ نرى عامة المسائل العلمية الاعتقادية برهانية الدليل والمسائل العمليَّة الفقهية دائرةً بين البرهاني وما يغلب فيه الظن غلبة تقترب من اليقين، إلا في فروع ليست بالكثيرة أمام حجم المستنبطات قد كانت في محل الاجتهاد، غير أن الأيام أظهرت أنها محصورة ضمن مذاهب أربعة قد تلقتها الأمة بالقبول، حتى كادت تحكم بخطأ ما سواها، ولا سيما بعد استقرار الفقه وأصوله، وغياب أهلية الاجتهاد. وليس المقصود من السواد الأعظم في الحديث الشريف ما كان في أصول الدين؛ ولذلك قال الإمام الجويني: (لا) معوّل على السواد الأعظم في أصل الدين؛ فإن سواد الكفرة أعظم من سوادنا، ولقد كان الرسول الله في صدر الإسلام في شرذمة قليلة العدد، وليس المعنى باتباع السواد الأعظم الاتباع في أصول الدين)(٢)، ومن هنا وجب تحريرُ الاعتقاد بالحجج والبراهين فلا يُرتضى إلا الاعتقاد الراسخ الذي هو اليقين.
And since branches have the ruling of the foundations, and the foundations of Ahl al-Sunna in creed (the foundations of religion and the science of kalam), jurisprudence (the foundations of fiqh and the foundations of hadith terminology), and spiritual education (the foundations of Sufism) are sound foundations clear in proof, the branches derived from them are sound by argument and proof, varying among themselves. For we see that most theoretical doctrinal issues are demonstrative in proof, while practical jurisprudential issues range from the demonstrative to what is preponderantly probable, close to certainty, except for a few branches, not many compared to the volume of derived rulings, which were subject to ijtihad. However, time has shown that they are confined to four schools that the community has accepted, to the point that they almost rule that other views are erroneous, especially after the stabilization of fiqh and its foundations, and the disappearance of the qualifications for ijtihad. And what is meant by the 'great majority' (al-sawad al-a'zam) in the noble hadith does not refer to matters of the foundations of religion. Therefore, Imam al-Juwayni said: 'No reliance is placed on the great majority in the foundation of religion; for the majority of the disbelievers is greater than our majority, and the Messenger of Allah, in early Islam, was with a small group of few number. The meaning of following the great majority is not following them in the foundations of religion.' And hence it is necessary to purify belief by proofs and demonstrations, so only the firm belief which is certainty is accepted.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This passage discusses the relationship between foundations and branches, and underscores the necessity of certain belief based on demonstration. The author begins by stating that branches of knowledge have the same ruling as their foundations. Since the foundations of Ahl al-Sunna—whether in creed (usul al-din and kalam), jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh and hadith methodology), or spiritual education (usul al-tasawwuf)—are sound and clearly evidenced, the branches derived from them are likewise sound through argument, though they vary in strength. Doctrinal issues are generally demonstrative (burhani), while practical fiqh issues range from demonstrative to strongly probable, except for a few minor branches that were open to ijtihad. Those branches, however, have become confined to the four accepted schools. The author then addresses the concept of 'al-sawad al-a'zam' (the great majority) mentioned in hadith. He argues that this does not apply to the fundamentals of religion. Citing al-Juwayni, he explains that the majority can be wrong—the majority of disbelievers is larger than the majority of believers, and the Prophet himself was with a small group early on. Therefore, following the majority is not a valid method for establishing creedal truths. Rather, one must purify one's belief through proofs and demonstrations, and only a firm, certain belief is acceptable. This refutes any reliance on mere numbers or consensus of the masses in doctrinal matters.

Key Terms
الفروع
الأصول
أصول الدين
الاجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the branches derived from Ahl al-Sunna's foundations sound?
A) Because they are accepted by the majority
B) Because the foundations themselves are sound and clear in proof
C) Because they have been approved by ijtihad
D) Because they are all demonstrative in nature

Key Takeaway
The authority of branches is derived from their foundations, and the soundness of Ahl al-Sunna's foundations ensures the soundness of their derived teachings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In which area of your life—your beliefs or your actions—are you following a 'branch' without having examined its 'root'? What concrete step will you take this week to trace that branch back to its foundation, using the method Ahl al-Sunna used?
?
The author says that many practical rulings are only preponderantly probable, close to certainty but not absolute. Which Islamic ruling do you treat as unquestionably certain in your daily practice that might actually belong to that probable category? How does that realization change the humility with which you should approach the people of knowledge?
?
You are reading this lesson after the stabilization of fiqh and the disappearance of ijtihad qualifications. Are you attached to one of the four schools? If not, what is the basis for your detachment? If yes, are you actively learning its foundations so that your practice is not blind imitation? Give yourself a measurable commitment today.

The Majority Is Not Proof; Certainty is Required
The author argues that the great majority has no bearing on creedal truth and asserts the need for certainty based on proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why numerical majority does not provide proof in matters of creed and why certainty is necessary for belief.

Core Idea
Truth is not determined by numbers.

In this passage, the author refutes the idea that the 'great majority' (al-sawad al-a'zam) is a valid proof in the foundations of religion. He quotes Imam al-Juwayni to show that the majority of disbelievers can be larger, and the Prophet himself began with a small group. Therefore, creedal truths must be established by proofs, not by following the crowd. The lesson concludes that only firm, certain belief is acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the clarity of al-Juwayni's refutation.
Pay attention to the two reasons given by al-Juwayni.
2
Understand al-Juwayni's argument
Al-Juwayni gives two reasons: the majority of disbelievers is greater than the majority of believers, and the Prophet started with a small group. Both show that numbers are not a criterion for truth.
3
Reflect on the necessity of certainty
The passage ends by stating that belief must be purified by proofs and only certain belief (yaqin) is acceptable. Think about how this standard affects the way we approach creedal issues.
Certainty here means firm conviction based on evidence, not blind faith.

Key Takeaway
Creedal truths are established by proof and demonstration, not by majority opinion; only certain belief is acceptable.

?

?
When was the last time you changed a belief or practice after examining the evidence, rather than following what was common? What would it take for you to stand alone on a truth, as the Prophet ﷺ and his early followers did?
?
You call yourself a Muslim—but is your faith based on certainty (yaqin) or on the comfort of being part of a large group? If your faith has never been tested by doubt or scrutiny, is it truly certain? Commit today to finding one proof for a belief you've always taken for granted.

Why Begin with Basmala and Hamdala?
Al-Lakani explains the poet's opening and clarifies a misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the poet opened his poem with basmala and hamdala, and the clarification that basmala was not the first revealed verse.

Core Idea
The basmala opens the poem as a sunnah of the Quran, not because it was first revealed.

The author begins by explaining the poet's choice to start with basmala and hamdala. This practice follows the Quran's own arrangement, but it is important to note that basmala was not the first revelation. A consensus of scholars affirms that all divine scriptures open with basmala, underscoring its universal significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the author's phrasing regarding the poet's opening and the reference to Sahih al-Bukhari.
Focus on the phrase 'لا أنهما أول ما أُنزل'.
2
Understand the Quranic order
The poet followed the Quran's fixed order (الترتيب التوقيفي) in placing basmala first, not because it was the first revealed verse.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.
3
Consider the consensus
Reflect on the transmitted consensus that all scriptures begin with basmala, showing its importance in divine revelation.
This is a key point for the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وها أنا أشرع في المقصود، بعون الملك المعبود، فأقول وبالله التوفيق: قوله: (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) افتتح الناظم كتابه بالبسملة ثم بالحمدلة اقتداءً بالكتاب العزيز في ابتدائه بهما في الترتيب التوقيفي، لا أنهما أول ما أُنزل؛ فإنه خلاف ما في صحيح البخاري وغيره في بدء الوحي من أن أول ما أنزل: {اقرأ باسم ربك} [العلق: 1]، وقد نقل أبو بكر التونسي إجماع علماء كل ملة على أن الله سبحانه وتعالى افتتح جميع كتبه بـ (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم)، وعملاً بخبر: كل أمر ذي بال لا يُبدأ فيه ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، فهو أبتر أو أجذم أو أقطع روايات؛ أي: ناقص وقليل البركة، فهو وإن تم حِساً، لا يتم معنى، مع خبر: كل أمر ذي بال لا يُبدأ فيه بالحمد لله ... إلى آخره. والمراد بالأمر: ما يعم القول كالقراءة، والفعل كالتأليف؛ ومعنى ذي بال: صاحب حال؛ بحيث يُهتم به شرعاً؛ أي بألا يكون من سفاسف الأمور، وليس محرماً ولا مكروهاً، ويشترط أيضاً ألا يكون ذكراً محضاً، ولا جعل الشارع له مبدأ.
And now I begin the intended purpose, with the help of the worshipped King, and I say, and with God is success: His statement: (In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful). The poet opened his book with the basmala then with the hamdala, following the Noble Book in its beginning with them in the fixed order, not that they are the first thing revealed; for that contradicts what is in Sahih al-Bukhari and others concerning the beginning of revelation, that the first thing revealed was 'Read in the name of your Lord' (Surah al-Alaq, 1). And Abu Bakr al-Tunisi transmitted the consensus of the scholars of every religious community that God Almighty opened all His books with 'In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful'. And acting upon the report: 'Every important matter that is not begun with "In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful" is severed, or maimed, or cut off' - variant narrations - meaning: deficient and of little blessing, for if it is complete in a sensory sense, it is not complete in meaning. Along with the report: 'Every important matter that is not begun with praise of God...' to the rest. And the meaning of 'matter' is what includes speech like reading, and action like authorship. And the meaning of 'important' (dhi bal) is: possessing a state, such that it is given importance according to Sharia; meaning that it should not be from the trivial matters, and it should not be forbidden nor disliked, and it is also a condition that it not be a mere remembrance (dhikr), nor that the Lawgiver has established a specific beginning for it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is the author's commentary on the basmala at the beginning of the poem. He explains that the poet (Ibn al-Lakani) started with basmala and hamdala, following the Qur'anic order of revelation (not that basmala was revealed first). He cites the hadith urging opening important matters with basmala, and explains the conditions: the matter must be important (not trivial), not forbidden or disliked, and not a purely devotional act (dhikr) that has its own prescribed beginning. He also notes a variant hadith about beginning with praise (hamd). The author defines 'أمر ذي بال' as any act that is given consideration by Sharia.

Key Terms
البسملة
الحمدلة
الترتيب التوقيفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the poet begin with basmala and hamdala?
A) Because they were the first revealed verses
B) Following the Quran's fixed order
C) Because he had no choice
D) As a personal habit

Key Takeaway
The poet opened with basmala and hamdala following the Quranic order, not because they were first revealed, and all scriptures begin with basmala.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day, do you consciously begin with the remembrance of Allah (like basmala) as a fixed priority, or do you allow your own whims to dictate the order? What one action will you take tomorrow to start something with 'Bismillah' with the awareness that you are following a divine pattern?
?
The poet corrected a misconception about what comes first. Are there beliefs or practices in your life that you have adopted because 'everyone does them' rather than because they are rooted in revelation? How will you investigate and realign them with the truth?
?
Allah opened all His books with 'In the name of God, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful'. Do you begin your speech, your work, and your relationships with this same consciousness of His mercy and grace? What would change if you consciously invoked His names before every significant action?

The Hadith on Beginning Important Matters with Basmala
Al-Lakani explains the hadith and conditions for basmala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith urging beginning important matters with basmala and its conditions, including the definition of 'amr dhi bal'.

Core Idea
Important matters must begin with basmala to attain blessing and completeness.

The author cites a hadith that every important matter should begin with basmala, otherwise it is deficient. He then explains the conditions for a matter to be considered 'important' (dhi bal), including that it is not trivial, not forbidden or disliked, not a pure dhikr, and not something with a divinely prescribed beginning.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic passage containing the hadith and its explanations carefully.
Note the variant terms: أبتر, أجذم, أقطع.
2
Understand the meaning of 'amr dhi bal'
The author defines 'amr' as general speech or action, and 'dhi bal' as matter of concern in Sharia, not trivial.
This definition is crucial for correct application.
3
Review the conditions
The author lists conditions: the matter must not be forbidden or disliked, not purely dhikr, and not have a prescribed starting formula.
These conditions limit the hadith's scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وها أنا أشرع في المقصود، بعون الملك المعبود، فأقول وبالله التوفيق: قوله: (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم) افتتح الناظم كتابه بالبسملة ثم بالحمدلة اقتداءً بالكتاب العزيز في ابتدائه بهما في الترتيب التوقيفي، لا أنهما أول ما أُنزل؛ فإنه خلاف ما في صحيح البخاري وغيره في بدء الوحي من أن أول ما أنزل: {اقرأ باسم ربك} [العلق: 1]، وقد نقل أبو بكر التونسي إجماع علماء كل ملة على أن الله سبحانه وتعالى افتتح جميع كتبه بـ (بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم)، وعملاً بخبر: كل أمر ذي بال لا يُبدأ فيه ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، فهو أبتر أو أجذم أو أقطع روايات؛ أي: ناقص وقليل البركة، فهو وإن تم حِساً، لا يتم معنى، مع خبر: كل أمر ذي بال لا يُبدأ فيه بالحمد لله ... إلى آخره. والمراد بالأمر: ما يعم القول كالقراءة، والفعل كالتأليف؛ ومعنى ذي بال: صاحب حال؛ بحيث يُهتم به شرعاً؛ أي بألا يكون من سفاسف الأمور، وليس محرماً ولا مكروهاً، ويشترط أيضاً ألا يكون ذكراً محضاً، ولا جعل الشارع له مبدأ.

The poet opened his book with the basmala then with the hamdala, following the Noble Book in its beginning with them in the fixed order, not that they are the first thing revealed; for that contradicts what is in Sahih al-Bukhari and others concerning the beginning of revelation, that the first thing revealed was 'Read in the name of your Lord' (Surah al-Alaq, 1). Along with the report: 'Every important matter that is not begun with praise of God...' to the rest. And the meaning of 'matter' is what includes speech like reading, and action like authorship. And the meaning of 'important' (dhi bal) is: possessing a state, such that it is given importance according to Sharia; meaning that it should not be from the trivial matters, and it should not be forbidden nor disliked, and it is also a condition that it not be a mere remembrance (dhikr), nor that the Lawgiver has established a specific beginning for it.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is the author's commentary on the basmala at the beginning of the poem. He explains that the poet (Ibn al-Lakani) started with basmala and hamdala, following the Qur'anic order of revelation (not that basmala was revealed first). He cites the hadith urging opening important matters with basmala, and explains the conditions: the matter must be important (not trivial), not forbidden or disliked, and not a purely devotional act (dhikr) that has its own prescribed beginning. He also notes a variant hadith about beginning with praise (hamd). The author defines 'أمر ذي بال' as any act that is given consideration by Sharia.

Key Terms
أمر ذي بال
ذِكر
أبتر
أجذم
أقطع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any matter whatsoever must be begun with basmala to be valid.
Correction: Only important matters (as defined in Sharia) require basmala; trivial, forbidden, or purely devotional acts are excluded.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for a matter to be considered 'dhi bal'?
A) Matter is not forbidden
B) Matter is not disliked
C) Matter is purely dhikr
D) Matter has no prescribed beginning

Key Takeaway
The hadith applies to important matters, defined by Sharia, excluding trivial, forbidden, disliked, pure dhikr, and acts with prescribed beginnings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an important task you have recently completed that you did not begin with basmala. How might that have affected the blessing and completeness of that task? What will you do tomorrow to ensure you remember basmala before your next important task?
?
The lesson teaches that even if an action is outwardly complete, it lacks meaning without basmala. Is there an area of your life where you focus on outward performance but neglect the inward blessing? Identify one such area and commit to starting with basmala from now on.
?
Consider an action you often do without basmala, like reading or starting a meeting. What stops you from making basmala a habit—forgetfulness or neglect? What one practical step will you take tonight to remind yourself to say basmala at the start of important matters tomorrow?

5 min
Reconciling Hadith on Basmala and Hamdala
Answers the objection of contradiction between two hadith by distinguishing real and additive beginnings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how apparent contradictions between two sound hadith can be resolved through the distinction between real and additive beginning (al-ibtida' al-haqiqi wa al-idafi).

Core Idea
Apparent hadith contradictions dissolve when we distinguish real beginning from additive beginning.

In this passage, the author addresses a potential objection: two authentic hadith praise different phrases (basmala and hamdala) for beginning acts, suggesting contradiction. He presents the most famous scholarly answer: 'beginning' is not one-dimensional. By distinguishing two meanings of beginning, the hadith are harmonized without rejecting either. This lesson walks you through that resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Start by reading the passage in Arabic and its translation. Notice how the objector frames the problem and the responder introduces the key distinction.
The objection is phrased as 'If you say...', typical kalam style.
2
Understand the two types of beginning
Focus on the definitions of real beginning (haqiqi) and additive beginning (idafi). Real: nothing precedes. Additive: something precedes but it's still considered a beginning.
These are technical terms with specific meanings in usul al-fiqh and hadith methodology.
3
See how the assignment resolves the conflict
Real beginning applies to the hadith on basmala; additive beginning applies to the hadith on hamdala. This assignment is supported by the Qur'an and consensus, not arbitrary.
The passage notes that reversing the assignment is not allowed due to textual and consensus evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت بين الخبرين المذكورين تعارض، فكيف يمكن العمل بهما ؟! :قلت أجيب عن ذلك بأجوبة، أشهرها : أن الابتداء نوعان: حقيقي؛ وهو الابتداء بما تقدَّمَ أمامَ المقصود ولم يسبقه شيء، وإضافيّ ؛ وهو الابتداء بما تقدَّمَ أمامَ المقصود وإن سبقه شيءٌ، فبينهما العموم والخصوص المطلق، فحمل خبر البسملة على النوع الأول، وخبر الحمدلة على النوع الثاني، وإنما لم يعكس للكتاب وللإجماع.
If you say: There is contradiction between the two mentioned reports, so how can both be acted upon? I say: It is answered with several answers, the most famous of which is that beginning is of two types: real beginning, which is beginning with what precedes the intended object and is not preceded by anything; and additive beginning, which is beginning with what precedes the intended object even if something preceded it. Between them is absolute generality and particularity. So the report of basmala is applied to the first type, and the report of hamdala to the second type. This was not reversed because of the Book and consensus.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector notes that two hadith—one praising basmala and the other praising hamdala for beginning acts—seem to contradict each other. The answer explains that 'beginning' (ibtida') can be understood in two ways: real (haqiqi) and additive (idafi). Real beginning is when nothing precedes the act; additive beginning is when something does precede the act but the act is still considered a beginning relative to what follows. The two hadith are reconciled by applying the hadith on basmala to real beginnings and the hadith on hamdala to additive beginnings. This assignment (not reversed) is supported by the Qur'an and consensus.

Key Terms
ابتداء حقيقي
ابتداء إضافي
العموم والخصوص المطلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two hadith are contradictory and one must be rejected.
Correction: They are reconciled by distinguishing real and additive beginnings, allowing both to be true.

Checkpoint
How are the two hadith on basmala and hamdala reconciled according to the passage?
A) One is abrogated
B) By distinguishing real vs. additive beginning
C) One applies to prayer, the other to general acts
D) They are both considered weak

Key Takeaway
The key to reconciling contradictory hadith is understanding that terms like 'beginning' can have multiple valid meanings, and each hadith applies to a specific context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an apparent contradiction in your own understanding of Islam—perhaps between mercy and justice, or between predestination and free will. How does the lesson's method of distinguishing different types of 'beginning' (or contexts) help you see that both can be true? What is one concrete step you will take this week to reconcile a perceived tension in your faith?
?
The passage required careful definition of the term 'beginning'. When you encounter a religious disagreement, do you first check how key terms are defined? If not, commit to defining terms before forming an opinion. What is one recurring disagreement you can approach with this method?
?
The scholar's answer allowed both hadith to be fully accepted. Are there any teachings you have dismissed because they seemed to conflict with others? Will you revisit them with the understanding that both might apply to different situations? Name one teaching you will reconsider.

The Ba in Basmala: Accompaniment or Seeking Help
Commentator explains two possibilities for the ba in basmala and prefers accompaniment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the commentator prefers the ba of accompaniment over seeking help in the basmala, and how this reflects the importance of adab in theological grammar.

Core Idea
Using God's name as a means risks discourtesy; accompaniment preserves reverence.

The basmala is central to Muslim life, but its grammatical meaning carries theological weight. Here the commentator examines two possibilities for the ba—accompaniment or seeking help—and argues for accompaniment to avoid implying that God's name is a mere instrument. This reveals how grammar and adab intersect in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the key terms: المصاحبة, الاستعانة, التبرك.
2
Identify the two meanings and the preference
Notice that the commentator presents two possibilities for the ba: accompaniment (for blessing) and seeking help. He then states his preference for accompaniment.
3
Understand the reasoning about discourtesy
The commentator argues that seeking help implies using God's name as an instrument, which is discourteous. Consider why this might be problematic in Islamic theology.
Think about the concept of adab (propriety) towards Allah.
4
Examine the counterargument and conclusion
The commentator acknowledges a counterargument that seeking help can be understood differently, but concludes that the likelihood of discourtesy remains.
Consider how the commentator prioritizes caution in matters of adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الباء في البسملة إما للمصاحبة على وجه التبرك، أو للاستعانة كذلك، ولا مانع من الاستعانة باسمه تعالى كما يستعان بذاته، والأولى جعلها للمصاحبة؛ لأن جعلها للاستعانة فيه إساءة أدب؛ لأنَّ باء الاستعانة تدخل على الآلة، فيلزم عليها جعل اسم الله مقصوداً لغيره لا لذاته إلا أن يقال: إن من جعلها للاستعانة نظر إلى جهة أخرى؛ وهي أن الفعل المشروع فيه لا يتم على الوجه الأكمل إلا باسمه تعالى، لكن قد يقال: مظنّة الإساءة ما زالت موجودة.
Then know that the ba in the basmala is either for accompaniment for the sake of blessing, or for seeking help likewise, and there is no impediment to seeking help by His name as help is sought by His essence. However, the better view is to make it for accompaniment because making it for seeking help involves discourtesy, because the ba of seeking help enters upon an instrument, so it would necessitate making the name of God intended for something other than itself. Unless it is said that the one who makes it for seeking help looks to another aspect, namely that the prescribed action is not completed in the most perfect way except by His name. But it might be said that the likelihood of discourtesy still exists.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage defines and evaluates the possible meanings of the ba in the basmala. The author states that the ba can indicate either accompaniment (musahaba) for blessing or seeking help (isti'ana) also for blessing. He notes that seeking help by God's name is permissible, just as seeking help by His essence. However, he argues that the preferable interpretation is accompaniment, because seeking help implies that the name is a means to an end, which could be disrespectful. He acknowledges a counterargument that seeking help can be understood differently, but maintains that the possibility of discourtesy remains, so accompaniment is safer.

Key Terms
الباء
المصاحبة
الاستعانة
التبرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that interpreting the ba as seeking help is equally valid and respectful.
Correction: The commentator argues that seeking help implies using God's name as an instrument, which is discourteous, so accompaniment is preferred.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer making the ba in basmala for accompaniment rather than seeking help?
A) Because seeking help is impermissible.
B) Because seeking help would imply that God's name is an instrument, which is discourteous.
C) Because the ba can only mean accompaniment.
D) Because seeking help is only for human actions.

Key Takeaway
The ba in basmala is preferably interpreted as accompaniment to avoid the discourtesy of using Allah's name as a mere instrument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'Bismillah' before an action, do you genuinely feel that you are accompanying Allah's name for blessing, or do you sometimes treat it as a tool to get your tasks done? How can you shift your intention today to be more reverent?
?
The commentator warns against using Allah's name as an instrument. Reflect on a moment you used His name casually or as a means to an end. What would it mean for you to now cultivate a sense of accompaniment in every 'Bismillah' that crosses your lips?
?
If you were to internalize that every word of Allah's name deserves inherent reverence, not utility, what would change about how you recite the basmala from now on? Write down one concrete commitment to avoid treating it as a mere ritual.

The Ishari Meaning of Basmala
Commentator explains the ishari meaning of basmala's ba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the symbolic interpretation of the ba in basmala as pointing to God's exclusive role in all existence and His perfect attributes.

Core Idea
The ba in basmala symbolically points to God as the source of all past and future existence.

This lesson explores a deeper layer of meaning in the basmala. The commentator moves beyond the literal reading and unveils an 'ishari' (symbolic) significance of the letter ba, connecting it directly to the foundations of Islamic belief about God's attributes and sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the core claim about the ba
The passage states that the ba indicates that by God was what was and will be what will be. Find this statement and reflect on its implications.
This is the central ishari meaning.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
The passage connects this meaning to all beliefs (aqa'id) and then to God's attributes of perfection and transcendence above deficiency. Ask yourself why this connection is made.
The ba's symbolism leads to tawhid and divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعناها الإشاري بي كان ما كان وبي يكون ما يكون، وحينئذ يكون في الباء إشارة إلى جميع العقائد؛ لأن المراد بي وجد ما وجد، وبي يوجد ما يوجد، ولا يكون كذلك إلا من اتَّصف بصفات الكمال وتنزّه عن صفات النقصان، كما ذكره بعض أئمة التفسير.
And its ishari meaning: by Him was what was, and by Him will be what will be. In that case, the ba contains an indication to all beliefs because the intended meaning is: by Him existed what existed, and by Him exists what exists. And this is not the case except for one who is described with attributes of perfection and is transcendent above attributes of deficiency, as some of the leading exegetes mentioned.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents the ishari (symbolic) interpretation of the ba in basmala. The commentator explains that the ba points to the truth that all things that have come into existence and all that will come into existence do so by God's power. This indicates that God is characterized by all perfect attributes and is free from all imperfections. The author attributes this interpretation to some leading Quranic exegetes.

Key Terms
التفسير الإشاري
العقائد
صفات الكمال
صفات النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The ishari meaning replaces or contradicts the literal meaning of basmala.
Correction: The ishari meaning is a deeper spiritual layer that coexists with the literal meaning, not a replacement.

Checkpoint
What does the ishari meaning of the ba in basmala indicate?
A) That God created only the past.
B) That everything past and future exists by God.
C) That God's name is a tool.
D) That only some things are by God.

Key Takeaway
The ba in basmala symbolically points to God as the sole cause of all existence and the possessor of perfect attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every moment of your existence is truly 'by Him', why do you still act as if your successes are your own doing? When will you start living in constant awareness that your next breath depends entirely on Him?
?
The ba points to God's perfect attributes—where in your life do you rely on your own flawed attributes instead of turning to His perfection? What deficiency are you still trying to hide behind?
?
If all beliefs rest on the truth that everything is by God, then what belief in your heart contradicts this? Is there an area of your life where you live as if something happens without His will? How will you realign that today?

The Recommendation to Begin with Praise (Hamdalah)
Nawawi quotes the recommendation to begin books and lessons with praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic recommendation to begin books and lessons with praise of Allah, as stated by Imam al-Nawawi.

Core Idea
Beginning with praise is a recommended practice.

In this lesson, we explore the ruling on starting written works and oral lessons with the hamdalah. Imam al-Nawawi’s statement provides the basis for this sunnah, which the author of the poem references.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage from Nawawi once without overanalyzing. Focus on the ruling (يستحب) and the contexts listed.
Notice the phrase 'يستحب الحمد' – the key term is istihbab (recommendation).
2
Identify the ruling and its scope
Identify that the ruling is recommendation (istihbab) and note the three contexts: authored books, teachers' lessons, and students' reading before teachers.
3
Reflect on the best wording
Observe that the best expression is 'الحمد لله رب العالمين' – this is the recommended phrase for praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الحَمْدُ اللهِ ... إلى آخره قال النووي رحمه الله تعالى : (يستحبُّ الحمدُ في ابتداء الكتب المصنفة، وكذا في ابتداء دروس المدرسين، وقراءة الطالبين بين يدي المعلمين، سواءٌ قرأ حديثاً أو فقهاً أو غيرَهُما ، وأحسنُ العبارات في ذلك : الحمد لله رب العالمين) انتهى (١). وإنما لم يأتِ بحرف العطف إشارة إلى أن كلا من البسملة والحمدلة محصل للمقصود في الابتداء، أو لاحتمال أن تكون إحداهما خبرية والأخرى إنشائية، والصحيحُ أنه لا يجوز عطفُ الإنشاء على الإخبار وعكسه.
His saying: 'Praise belongs to God... etc.' Al-Nawawi (may God have mercy on him) said: 'It is recommended to praise God at the beginning of authored books, and likewise at the beginning of teachers' lessons, and the reading of students in front of teachers, whether it is a hadith or fiqh or other, and the best expressions for that is: Praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.' End. And he (the author) did not come with a conjunction indicating that each of the basmala and hamdalah achieves the intended purpose in the beginning, or because one of them may be declarative and the other performative, and the correct view is that it is not permissible to conjoin the performative to the declarative or vice versa.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage begins with the author commenting on the opening verse of the poem: "الحمد لله". He quotes Imam al-Nawawi to establish the recommendation (istihbab) of beginning books and lessons with praise. Then he states that the author of the poem omitted the conjunction between the basmala and the hamdala, indicating that either one suffices for the purpose of beginning. Al-Sanusi then explains that the reason for the lack of conjunction could also be grammatical: one expression is declarative (khabariyya) and the other is performative (insha'iyya), and it is not allowed to conjoin a performative to a declarative or vice versa.

Key Terms
الحمد
الحمدلة
يستحب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Nawawi, what is the ruling on beginning books or lessons with praise of Allah?
A) Obligatory (wajib)
B) Recommended (mandub)
C) Permissible (mubah)
D) Disliked (makruh)

Key Takeaway
It is recommended to begin books and lessons with praise of Allah, and the best phrase is 'الحمد لله رب العالمين'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you begin to study or teach, do you consciously say 'الحمد لله رب العالمين'? If not, what is one specific change you will make starting from your next session?
?
This lesson teaches that praising Allah at the start is recommended, not obligatory. Does knowing that this is a sunnah (not a burden) make you more eager to practice it, or does it reduce your motivation? Be honest with yourself.
?
Imagine you are about to write an email, prepare a lesson, or even start a conversation about deen. Will you remember to begin with praise? What is one practical step you can take today to make this sunnah a habit?
